A Glimmer of Hope for the Cotton Textile Industry 46

The Social Affairs Bureau Will Hold a Meeting

The crisis in the local cotton textile industry has been evident in recent years, with closures following one another. The industry's trade association has repeatedly requested relief from the Social Affairs Bureau. The Social Affairs Bureau believes that the fundamental relief still lies in solving all the current difficulties of the cotton textile industry, which is beyond the ability of a single city. It has submitted a request to the Municipal Government to consult the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for overall planning and review. After receiving a reply from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce that it has a plan, it has consulted the Municipal Government and scheduled a meeting of factory owners to discuss concrete plans. The various news reports are recorded as follows: The Ministry of Industry and Commerce's reply to the Municipal Government: Regarding the matter of reply, according to the previous requests from the Municipal Business Consolidation Committee and the Social Affairs Bureau for relief of the cotton textile industry's dangerous situation, in addition to requesting the Ministry of Finance to reduce and exempt taxes and ordering the National Goods Bank to provide financial assistance, it is proposed to order the Social Affairs Bureau to inform the workers not to rush to request wage increases and to maintain the status quo, and to convene manufacturers to study ways to circulate accumulated goods in order to achieve the effect of official and commercial cooperation. As per the consultation, please check and handle. The Social Affairs Bureau Schedules a Meeting: After the Social Affairs Bureau received the instructions from the Municipal Government, and at the same time, it received a request from the local cotton textile workers' union to support workers and promote national goods in order to maintain the cotton textile industry, the bureau decided to convene a meeting of factory owners at the bureau at 9:00 AM on the 28th of this month in order to discuss concrete plans. It has already instructed the industry's trade association to forward the notice yesterday.

The Trade Association Discusses Proposals: The industry's trade association has been requesting relief since it first submitted the request for relief, and in the blink of an eye, a year has passed. The crisis is even worse, and the general members and manufacturers are all worried. After receiving the instructions from the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, it was scheduled to hold a members' meeting at the Ruilin Li Association on Edward Road at 12:00 PM on today (26th) to discuss in detail the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's relief measures and management methods, and then submit a proposal to the Social Affairs Bureau to be included in the agenda.

江浙絲綢織機聯合會 47

Emergency Meeting Minutes

The Jiang-Zhe Silk Loom Association has recently received reports from fellow merchants in various districts of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces stating that this year's silkworm cocoon harvest is poor, raw materials are severely lacking, and foreign firms are competing to purchase fresh cocoons and transport them overseas, resulting in a decrease in silk reeling. Our country's silk industry is facing a shortage of raw materials, industrial stagnation, and soaring silk prices, which have reached a high of two and a half fields. There is a continued upward trend in prices. At a time when the nation is advocating for domestic goods amidst the trend of financial stringency, costs should be reduced, and everyone should work together. However, due to the high cost of silk, the current selling price of silk fabrics does not cover the costs, resulting in significant losses for silk factories, increased closures, and growing unemployment. For the sake of preserving the industry, it seems appropriate to consider increasing the selling price to sustain the industry. Matters concerning how to alleviate the silk cocoon raw material shortage, reduce unreasonable taxes, and promote domestic silk fabrics must be discussed in a general meeting and implemented after a public resolution. Therefore, a joint meeting of silk merchants from the two provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang was convened on the 22nd. The representatives from the provinces who attended were: (1) Suzhou silk industry representatives: Shi Junqing, Yu Wenqing, Chen Guiting, Cheng Lisheng, Ma Yangshi, Yao Keshen, Wang Shengshan, Liu Guangyuan; Shanghai representatives: Wang Xingyi, Xu Wenbing, Wang Shoushen, Gu Shenglu; (2) Hangzhou silk industry representatives: Lu Zhengbing (represented by Tu Shuqing), Ye Jinkang, Chen Jianming, Yang Hanqing; (3) Huzhou silk industry representatives: Pan Yisheng, Fei Rongfang, Xu Jinsheng, Wang Hesun; (4) Shengjing silk industry representatives: Wang Shaocun, Cheng Huisheng; (5) Danyang silk industry representative: Zhou Lianbo. The meeting commenced at 3 PM with the ringing of a bell. Wang Jie'an was elected as chairman. After following the formal opening procedures, Sun Zheng recorded the minutes. The chairman announced the purpose of the meeting and read letters from fellow merchants in the two provinces, detailing the industry's decline and precarious situation in recent years. It was stated that unless the merchants of the two provinces unite and discuss ways to alleviate the suffering, and request the government to implement effective measures, the crisis cannot be averted. After considering various proposals, the following resolutions were made: (1) New pricing proposal: The entire assembly voted to temporarily increase the price by one and a half points starting July 1st, as per the spring market, and to publish this in the newspapers (local and foreign). Future discussions will be held to further address this. (2) Alleviating the silk cocoon raw material shortage: It was resolved to petition the government to reiterate the restriction on establishing new cocoon businesses in the old nine prefectures of the two provinces (Suzhou, Ningbo, Changzhou, and Zhenjiang in Jiangsu; Hangzhou, Jiaxing, Huzhou, Ningbo, and Shaoxing in Zhejiang), as per previous decisions. (3) Promoting domestic silk fabrics: It was resolved to petition the government, in conjunction with the China National Products Preservation Association, to explicitly restrict the use of Western clothing and implement Article 6 of the Clothing System Regulations, which limits the use of domestic goods and imposes penalties on violators. (4) Petitioning the government to establish a national artificial silk factory: The resolution was passed. (5) Reducing taxes on domestic silk fabrics: It was resolved to petition the government to exempt all taxes to alleviate the burdens on the silk industry. (6) Revising the Factory Law provisions: It was resolved to petition the government to revise Article 1 of Chapter 1 of the law (which applies to factories that regularly employ 30 or more workers), changing the number "30" to "1,000" to better suit the conditions of small-scale industrial factories in the country. After the discussions, refreshments were served, and the meeting was adjourned with the ringing of a bell at around 6 PM.

Petitioning to the Capital 48

Cigarette Industry Representatives Detail Grievances

Party and Government Organs Express Support

Representatives from the Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Factory Guild, facing potential bankruptcy due to raw material shortages, foreign taxes, and pricing issues, were dispatched to the capital on the 23rd. This delegation, consisting of Lang Tingsheng, Shen Xingde, and Liu Chenglong (representing the Guangdong Guild), carried letters to various ministries to present their case. This newspaper has extensively reported on this matter. It is now known that Yu Qiaqing, a member of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's committee handling this case, also arrived in Beijing on the same day. On the morning of the 24th, the representatives visited the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, where they were received by Vice Minister Mu Ouchu and Director Zhang Yiou. The representatives passionately described the current difficulties faced by the cigarette industry and provided evidence of their inability to sustain operations, requesting urgent assistance. Vice Minister Mu and Director Zhang responded that the Ministry had been aware of the difficulties faced by the Chinese cigarette industry and that the issues raised in the petition were valid. They stated that since a specific request had been made, they would work with the Ministry of Finance to find appropriate solutions and provide practical assistance. However, they emphasized that the Chinese cigarette industry should cultivate a long-term vision, consolidate its strength, and seek commercial advantages through unity, as businesses that neglect the power of unity ultimately fail. They hoped this would serve as a lesson. In the afternoon, the representatives visited the Executive Yuan, where they were received by Liu Gongqian, the Chairman's Secretary. They reiterated their grievances as described above. Liu responded that the Executive Yuan was aware of the extreme distress faced by the Chinese cigarette industry and had already planned to work with the Ministries of Industry and Commerce and Finance to develop solutions to alleviate the crisis, aid the development of the industry, and ensure the well-being of the people. The representatives then departed after expressing their concerns. Subsequent news indicated that the association's representatives visited the Central Party Headquarters on the morning of the 25th to submit their petition.

Page 14

Nineteenth Year of the Republic of China

Mr. Zhou Zhongmei was assigned to receive them. The situation appeared to be promising, and the Standing Committee would consider providing further assistance. It was also reported that a petition to the Ministry was scheduled for today.

Domestic Towels Granted Tax Exemption 49

Subject to Certification by the Industry Association

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously forwarded a petition from the National Towel Industry Association requesting tax exemptions for domestically produced towels to promote their sales. This petition has now been approved. The association's letter to the National Towel Industry Association is quoted below: "On the 18th of this month, we received an electric message from the Ministry of Finance, forwarded through the Chamber of Commerce, regarding the request by the Shanghai National Towel Industry Association to exempt domestic towels from internal taxes. The three ministries have instructed the Special Commissioner of Finance for Jiangsu Province to review the matter and submit a response. According to the response received, 'We have received Order No. 14518 from your ministry, forwarding the request from the Shanghai National Towel Industry Association, via an electric message from the Shanghai Special Municipality Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee, to exempt domestic towels from internal taxes, instructing this office to review the matter and submit a response.' Upon receiving this order, we promptly complied. We also received a petition from representatives of the association, including Zhang Zilian, stating that domestic towels are taxed on raw materials, semi-finished products, finishing, printing, transportation, and sales, resulting in excessively high costs and difficult sales, which is a realistic situation. Machine-made towels have already been exempted from taxes upon petition. The majority of these domestic towels are produced in family industries. The question of whether internal taxes can be exempted or modified has been referred to the Special Tax Bureau, which has summoned representatives of the industry to inquire and discuss a compromise. According to the response received, the annual output of domestic towels in this province is approximately one million dozens, with roughly half being sold domestically and half being exported. The majority of production is concentrated in Baoshan, Chuansha, Nanhui, Chongming, Jiading, and Pudong in Shanghai, with some production in Gangshan, Zhenjiang, and Nanjing. In addition, many other counties produce towels in similar family industries for local consumption. Except for local sales and small-scale carrying, which are not reported for taxation, all towels produced by large and small factories and family industries in Baoshan, Chuansha, Nanhui, Chongming, Jiading, and Pudong around Shanghai are transported as semi-finished products for finishing or transported to Shanghai for finishing, printing, and then wholesaled to various ports. As such, wholesale centers for these towels are concentrated in Shanghai. When wholesaling and transshipping, they are often packed in boxes with various cotton fabrics or foreign goods. In the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, the total towel tax in the province, excluding customs duties, was 3,634 yuan, 7 jiao, 4 fen, and 6 li. This refers specifically to towels reported for transportation; items bundled in boxes are taxed based on an estimated rate per item and are not included. However, cotton goods such as gloves, socks, scarves, and undershirts are daily necessities and are often produced in family industries. It is not just towels that face this issue. If towels are exempted from taxes, there will inevitably be a cascade of requests for similar exemptions, which is difficult to deny. Moreover, towels that have been exempted from taxes, when bundled with various cotton goods for shipment to various ports, may be falsely declared as foreign goods or may be mixed with items that have not been exempted from taxes. If tax authorities were to inspect each box, the procedures would become even more difficult, and merchants might use this as an excuse to create unnecessary trouble, ultimately impacting tax revenues. After receiving the order, the committee repeatedly summoned representatives, including Zhang Zilian, to conduct further inquiries and detailed discussions. It was generally agreed that not exempting taxes would make it impossible for the industry to survive, while granting a general exemption would lead to various disputes that are difficult to prevent and would be self-inflicted trouble. The only solution is to carefully consider the situation and make a flexible compromise to reduce taxes, so as to not hinder either national revenue or industry. Considering the tax revenue in the eighteenth year, a large portion comes from towels produced in Baoshan, Chuansha, Nanhui, Chongming, Jiading, and Pudong and transported to Shanghai for finishing and wholesaling. Wholesaling from Shanghai to other ports still requires bundling and reporting for taxation, so the issue of double taxation cannot be ignored. Special taxes were originally separated from the Likin tax, so comprehensive consideration should be given to both. Furthermore, with the clear order to abolish the Likin tax in October of this year, goods exempted from taxes should be included in the abolished Likin tax plan. During this transition period, it is proposed that large and small factories and family industries in Baoshan, Chongming, Jiading, Chuansha, Nanhui, and Pudong be required to have a certificate from the Towel Industry Association verifying that the goods are not of inferior quality and are indeed being transported for finishing and wholesaling, before being inspected and released without taxation. Shipments from Shanghai to other ports, whether transported individually or bundled, and goods that the association believes are being transported with inferior products or goods for which the association refuses to issue a certificate, should be taxed according to regulations. This approach avoids double taxation, simplifies inspection, and prevents the passing off of foreign goods as domestic goods. This provides special consideration for family industries while also requiring manufacturers and businesses to fulfill their tax obligations. This approach aligns with the Ministry's intention to promote domestic goods. We have attached a sample certificate form to the report for review. It seems appropriate to approve the proposed method of taxing domestic towels, with tax exemptions for goods being transported for finishing and wholesaling, and to have the Towel Industry Association issue certificates to prevent fraud, as well as the proposed certificate form. Please review and approve accordingly. To the National Towel Industry Association.

Ham Industry 50

Opposing Increased Taxes in Zhejiang Province

Petitioning for the Zhejiang Provincial Government to Rescind the Taxes

Jinhua, Zhejiang province, is the primary producer of ham. Last year, the local ham industry experienced a decline due to various factors. In June of this year, the Zhejiang Department of Finance suddenly announced an increase in taxes, prompting widespread opposition. Local ham merchants also submitted a petition to the Municipal Party Department and the Chamber of Commerce, requesting them to forward the petition to the Zhejiang Provincial Government to rescind the newly established tax rates. The petition is quoted below: "Regarding the illegal increase in ham taxes by Zhejiang province, which exceeds the previous tax rate by one and a half times, we request you to forward this to the Zhejiang Provincial Government to rescind the new tax rate, in order to benefit the people and alleviate commercial hardship. Before the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, the ham and cured meat tax in Zhejiang province was 6 fen of silver for each ham and 8 jiao and 4 fen of silver for every hundred catties of cured meat. In the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, it was changed to 9 fen of silver for each ham and 1 yuan and 2 jiao and 6 fen of silver for every hundred catties of cured meat. The people already found this to be an unbearable burden. The Zhejiang Department of Finance suddenly issued a notice stating that, starting from June 1st of this year, the tax would be changed to 1 jiao and 5 fen of silver for each ham and 1 jiao and 5 fen of silver for every ten catties of cured meat. In addition, the Zhejiang West Water Conservancy fee of 7 li and 5 hao is added when passing through Zhejiang West, which is more than one and a half times the tax rate before the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, and even compared to the current tax rate, it is an increase of 40 percent. What is the purpose of this? It is incomprehensible. At a time when there is no change in the taxation of all goods, the tax on ham has increased by 40 percent, which is clearly inappropriate. Ham production in Jinhua, Lanxi, Dongyang, Yiwu, Yongkang, and Pujiang counties in eastern Zhejiang is of great importance to the livelihoods of the people. Farmers in the region rely on raising pigs to obtain fertilizer, which directly and indirectly benefits agricultural production. Therefore, they view raising pigs as a secondary occupation. Beans, wheat bran, and husks can be used as pig feed, and pig urine and manure can be used as fertilizer for fields, creating a cycle of mutual benefit. Recently, there has been a tooth tax on buying pigs and a slaughter tax on killing pigs. Repeated exploitation has made it difficult to raise pigs for fertilizer. Since fertilizer is not easily obtained, there is no hope for a bumper harvest of crops, and farmers are forced to purchase imported fertilizer powder to replace it, leading to an outflow of money and hardship for farmers. This is a cause for concern among those who understand the situation. Now, the repeated increase in tax rates is akin to driving fish into the deep. The silk industry in western Zhejiang has been squeezed by foreign goods, leading to a decline in the market. To save domestic products, the Zhejiang Provincial Government has reduced the annual silk tax from 840,000 yuan to 440,000 yuan since last winter. Ham and silk are both products of Zhejiang province, but their tax rates are increasing for one and decreasing for the other. Are the people of eastern and western Zhejiang fortunate and unfortunate, respectively? The association has witnessed the difficulties of the times and fears that if the provincial government does not protect ham, it will be destroyed. In ten or twenty years, there will be no families raising pigs or businesses pickling ham, let alone tax revenue. The harms of official and civilian contributions are obvious. Therefore, we are detailing the reasons and requesting your association to forward this to the Zhejiang Provincial Government, requesting them to rescind the newly established tax rates to alleviate the hardship of the people and maintain commercial stability (remainder omitted)."

Promulgation by the Jiangsu Civil Affairs Department 51

Methods for Selecting County Police Chiefs

The Shanghai County Government yesterday received Instruction No. 3753 from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs, stating that: "In order to comply with the County Police Force Organization Temporary Regulations, which were previously promulgated, the county police force is the dedicated organization in each county responsible for suppressing bandits and making arrests. The police chief is responsible for local security, and their responsibilities are extremely important. Therefore, strict selection is necessary to promote genuine talent and prevent those who seek advancement through improper means. We have now established temporary methods for selecting county police chiefs for your reference. We are issuing a copy of the methods and instructing the county magistrate to promptly inform all parties." Included is a copy of the temporary methods for selecting county police chiefs in Jiangsu province.

Temporary Methods for Selecting County Police Chiefs in Jiangsu Province: (Article 1) The appointment of county police chiefs in Jiangsu province, unless otherwise stipulated by law, will be provisionally governed by these selection methods. (Article 2) The selection committee will be temporarily appointed by the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs. (Article 3) Individuals who have not passed the selection process are not eligible to be appointed as county police chief. (Article 4) All incumbent county police chiefs, except those who have already been trained or assessed as qualified, must be transferred to the province in batches for assessment in accordance with these methods. (Article 5) Candidates for county police chief must meet one of the following qualifications: (1) Graduates of a formal military academy with police expertise. (2) Those who have served in military positions with the rank of field officer or higher for two years or more, or in police positions with commissioned rank or higher for one year or more. (3) Graduates of a police academy for three years or more with military skills. (4) Graduates of a police academy for one year or more who have served in military positions with the rank of captain or higher for two years or more. (Article 6) Applicants must submit their resumes, supporting documents, a recent 2.5-inch portrait photo, and a guarantee from a substantive official of the province with the rank of Recommended Appointment or higher, guaranteeing that they do not have any of the following circumstances: (1) Engaging in counter-revolutionary activities. (2) Being expelled or suspended from the Party without being reinstated. (3) Engaging in corruption or bullying local people. (4) Being subject to dismissal with confirmed evidence. (5) Defaulting on public funds or failing to settle accounts. (6) Smoking opium or being physically weak and unable to perform their duties. (Article 7) Applicants must undergo academic and practical skills assessments and oral examinations: (1) Academics: Party principles, essentials of police work, model orders. (2) Practical skills: Real-troop command (battalion and company command actions). (3) Oral examination. (Article 8) Supporting documents will be returned after review and assessment. All qualified personnel, whether incumbent or not, will either return to their original positions or be recorded for priority appointment. (Article 9) These methods will be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Import, Export, and Transit

Food Inspection and Registration Regulations of the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining

Approved by the Central Political Council

The Central Political Council has approved the import, export, and transit food inspection and registration regulations based on the recommendations of the Food Committee and has instructed the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining to order agricultural product inspection offices or local governments to implement them. As previously reported, Shanghai, being the primary port for import, export, and transit of food, should prioritize inspection and registration to regulate food supply in the Yangtze River provinces. Upon receiving the order from the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining immediately instructed the Shanghai Agricultural Product Inspection Office, under Director Jin Wensi, to prepare accordingly. Director Jin contacted leading rice merchants in Shanghai, including Ye Huijun, to discuss inspection and registration procedures. The office drafted the Shanghai Import, Export, and Transit Food Inspection and Registration Regulations and submitted them to the Ministry of Agriculture. The Ministry then revised the regulations, changing "rice" to "food" to make them applicable to inspection and registration agencies in all ports. The revised regulations were submitted to the Executive Yuan for record-keeping. Considering the national importance of food supply, the Executive Yuan deemed the matter too important for a simple proclamation and forwarded it to the National Government for consideration by the Central Political Council. The Central Political Council then referred it to the Food Committee for review. The Food Committee's specialists made minor revisions and submitted the regulations to the Central Political Council for approval before being officially promulgated by the National Government. The Ministry of Agriculture and Mining has already instructed the agricultural product inspection office to establish a special task force to prepare actively. The regulations will be implemented as soon as they are promulgated by the Ministry.

Shanghai-Chengdu Aviation Administration Abolished 56

All Stations to Cease Operations

Beijing-Shanghai Flights to Continue as Usual

The Ministry of Communications and the China National Aviation Corporation have jointly agreed to reorganize the internal operations and routes of both aviation businesses. After a week of meetings with representatives from both sides, an agreement has been reached. It is understood that the China National Aviation Corporation will be expanded, and the Shanghai-Chengdu Aviation Administration established by the Ministry of Communications will be abolished and merged into the corporation, becoming China's share capital. In the future, the internal organization and administrative powers of the merged company will belong to the Board of Directors, whose members will be appointed by the National Government. The terms of the agreement have been drafted by the Ministry of Communications and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval by the National Government. It is now known that the Shanghai-Chengdu Aviation Administration has received instructions from the Ministry of Communications to cease operations by the end of this month. Upon receiving the order, Director Nie Kaiyi instructed all staff to expedite the closure and ordered the Shanghai, Nanjing, and Hankou stations, as well as the three radio stations in Shanghai, Beijing, and Hankou, and the Jiujiang Administration, to cease operations simultaneously pending transfer. It is reported that the Beijing-Shanghai flights will continue as usual during the closure period. It is also reported that the employees of the stations will be retained or transferred to work for the company. The administration has been in operation for just over a year.

Update on the French Concession Water and Electricity Workers' Strike 57

Workers' Union Issues Announcement to Dispel Rumors

This newspaper has reported extensively on the strike by the French Concession Water and Electricity Workers' Union. It has now learned that the union recently heard that a Sichuanese man, Zhang Shigen, threw stones at a trolley bus traveling from Xujiahui to Sixteen Pu Second Road at the intersection of Father Labour Road and Luban Road at around 10:00 PM the night before. He was arrested by French police and sent to the Lujiawan Police Station for processing. The union stated that since the start of the strike, the workers have followed the orders of the higher authorities and have not taken any improper actions. Fearing that external rumors might distort the truth and hinder the labor movement, the union issued an urgent announcement to solemnly declare that Zhang Shigen is not a member of the union and that the stone-throwing incident was carried out by reactionary elements. They urged the authorities to severely punish the perpetrator. Trolley Buses Cannot Traverse Two Concessions

Trolley buses originally traveled through the British Concession. However, since the strike, many trolley buses have been damaged, and only a few are operating, resulting in irregular service through the British Concession. Fearing accidents, the British Concession has temporarily suspended the operation of trolley buses from the French Concession, including lines 14, 17, and 18, from entering the British Concession, starting from 2:00 PM the day before. Similarly, British Concession trolley buses are not operating in the French Concession. It is feared that service cannot be restored until after the strike is resolved.

Conclusion of Debate in the 62

Judgment on July 1st

The case of Zhang Taijie, manager of the Sichuan Road Company, being sued by Zeng Xianzhi, the representative of the directors, in the Local Court for embezzlement of road funds and property, was continued yesterday morning at 10:00 am by Chief Judge Shen Bingrong, together with assessors Wu Zhen and Qian Chengjun, in the First Tribunal. However, since the lawyer can represent, he can represent taking the money. There is no need to send someone else. He requests that it be judged according to the law." After the first defense, the judge announced the conclusion of the public prosecution debate and began the private prosecution trial. Regarding this case, we request that the court order the recovery of 17 Hanyeping shares, one Qinghua Company IOU and its attached shares, and Cheng Xuelou's loan of 34,000 taels. If they cannot be handed over, they should be ordered to repay 485,850 taels and 4 qian and 8 fen of silver." The judge questioned Zhang Taijie, who claimed that the plaintiff was not qualified to make this claim and had nothing to say. The judge then announced the conclusion of the debate and ordered the defendant Zhang Taijie to be returned to custody for sentencing at 11:00 am on July 1st.

Shanghai Club Secretary Maisbale 63

Dies Tragically from a Gunshot Wound on His Birthday

The Birthday Feast Was Not Held Before the Birthday Star Passed Away

He Has a Wife in His Hometown and a Lover in Shanghai

A Mystery of Accidental Killing or Suicide

Canadian C.W. Maisbale, who has been working as the secretary of the Shanghai Club at 3 The Bund for many years, was to celebrate his 55th birthday yesterday. Relatives and friends were planning to hold a birthday celebration for Mr. Maisbale in the evening. However, before the birthday feast could be held, the tragic news arrived first. Maisbale committed suicide in his private room at sunset. The news spread, and everyone was amazed. According to the servants, Mr. Mai was alone in his private room after lunch. The servants dared not enter without being called. At about 2:00 pm, Mr. Mai ordered his attendant to prepare machine oil for him. He also ordered the tobacconist to bring cigarettes. His attitude was leisurely and did not seem like he was about to face a major disaster. At about 4:50 pm, the attendant entered his private room again and saw Mr. Mai carefully wiping his gun with machine oil. Half an hour later, the tragedy suddenly occurred. A loud bang was heard from the room, followed by a loud sound. More than a dozen servants were working in the room next to Mai's residence. Hearing the sound, they rushed to Mai's room and opened the door. They saw the birthday star lying stiff on the ground, with bloodstains all over his chest, moaning non-stop. The manager quickly summoned a doctor for emergency treatment, but it was too late. Mr. Mai had already passed away by the time the doctor arrived. The bullet entered from the right chest and did not exit. After receiving the news, detectives were dispatched to investigate. They saw the deceased lying stiff on the ground, with a Hebble-style .45 caliber pistol beside him. It was not certain whether it was suicide or accidental killing. Mr. Mai's wife lives in his hometown in Canada, and they still exchanged letters a month ago. However, Mai had another lover in Shanghai, living at 12 Gongguan Road in the French Concession. He died tragically from a gunshot wound on his birthday. Even if it was not suicide, this ending is still tragic.

More Than a Dozen Boxes of 64

Tung Oil Turned into Clear Water

Boatmen Collude in Fraud

Exposure Due to Uneven Distribution of Spoils

In May of this year, the Portuguese company Baoli Yanghang entrusted Chen Jiangji Lighter Company to transport 116 barrels of tung oil to the Japanese ship Kinzan Maru to be shipped overseas. The company sent boatmen Shi Jinchu, Chen Yinchu, Zhang Linxuan, Sun Chuanjiang, etc. to load onto the ship. Due to customs inspection, the loading was not completed until the 12th. They then transported the boat to Xiqiong Port and opened 24 barrels of tung oil, pouring the oil into another boat and filling the empty barrels with clear water. Then they nailed them shut and mixed them in with the tung oil, successfully smuggling them onto the ship, which has already sailed overseas. In total, more than 4,000 yuan worth of tung oil was stolen. However, because there were more than a dozen people involved and the spoils were not distributed evenly, an anonymous letter was sent to the foreign company, who reported it to the Water Patrol Police Station for investigation. Detectives Wang Haiquan, Ge Changsheng, and Shen Agui were dispatched and arrested Shi Jinchu, Chen Yinchu, Zhang Linxuan, Sun Chuanjiang, etc. They also telegraphed the Kinzan Maru to inquire. The ship replied that after unpacking, more than 20 boxes were indeed clear water. The case was then revealed. Yesterday, the head constable issued an order for the detectives to transfer the defendants to the Local Court for trial.

Superstition is Difficult to Break for a While 65

A Torch of More Than a Hundred Yuan

Unceasing Remembrance of the Deceased Wife

Burning a Gorgeous Paper House

Wang Songsong, a resident of the last house in the first alley of Xin Xieye Lane, South City River Road, Wusong, lost his wife, Gu, to illness last month. When Gu was alive, her relationship with Wang was extremely harmonious. Therefore, Wang was very saddened by Gu's death. Yesterday was the fifth seventh-day memorial service after Gu's death. Wang, unable to comfort his feelings, specially hired Taoist priests to perform rituals at his home and ordered a large paper house from a paper crafts shop, costing about a hundred yuan. The paper house was fully equipped with various furnishings and was extremely grand and gorgeous. At about 5:00 pm yesterday, a fire was lit on the vacant lot east of the Wusong Town Station to burn it. The flames soared into the sky, resembling a fire alarm. It took about an hour to burn completely. A large crowd gathered to watch the spectacle.

Dare to Terrify Xu, the Bandit Is Bold 66

Sending a Threatening Letter to the Door

Contacted Four Times Before and After

The Person Involved Has Gone to Beiping

Bandit Li Afu Arrested

Ren Boxuan, residing at 505 Datong Road, suddenly received a threatening letter on the 8th of this month demanding 12,000 yuan. Ren smiled and ignored it. However, on the 14th, he received another letter from the bandits demanding the same amount as before. Ren sent the two letters to the Xinzha Police Station for investigation and immediately set off for Beiping to avoid harassment. However, on the 19th, the bandits sent a third letter to Ren, stating that they would meet at the entrance of the Jing'an Temple at 9:00 am on the 20th. Ren's family sent Jin Afu as agreed. Jin returned and reported that he arrived at the agreed location shortly before encountering a bandit. They began negotiations, but because the two sides could not agree on the amount, they changed the appointment to between 7:00 and 8:00 am on the 21st in front of a teahouse on Hart Road. Ren's family reported this to the police station, who sent detectives to accompany Jin. They did not see anything. Until the day before yesterday (the morning of the 23rd), the bandits sent a person to Ren's back door to sneakily insert a letter through the door seam. Fearing that his family would not know, they rang the doorbell installed at the door and knocked loudly on the door. The people in the house heard the sound and opened the door, picking up the bandit's fourth letter from the ground, stating that they would meet at the entrance of the Vatican Palace on Route Sainte-Marie in the French Concession between 6:00 and 7:00 pm that day. Ren's family changed the representative to Zhu Baosheng to meet and talk. The bandits demanded 10,000 yuan, and Zhu agreed to 6,000 yuan, but still without result. They re-appointed at the end of Datong Road on Baker Road at 10:00 am on the 24th. At that time, the police station sent Chinese and foreign detectives to ambush around. Zhu held a newspaper in one hand as a sign and held a paper bag in the other hand, pretending to be banknotes. Shortly after, Li Afu, a Hangzhou native from the bandit side, swaggered over and talked to Zhu. He was then arrested by the detectives and sent to the Special District Local Court yesterday. Judge Wu interrogated him, and police station lawyer Ru Bao Yi explained the process. The defendant also confessed without denying. Judge Wu ordered the defendant to be detained and rescheduled the trial for the morning of July 4th.

Domestic Soap Will Increase in Price Again 71

To Be Implemented from July 10th

Due to the high cost of raw materials, the domestic soap industry previously announced a price increase through the industry association. Yesterday, the association stated that the source of raw materials is becoming increasingly scarce and the price of gold is rising every day. Calculating the cost according to the previous price is not enough. It was decided to increase the price again after consultation with the industry. The amount of the increase will temporarily be based on the previous increase as a standard. Although it is still not enough to make up for the losses, the industry association announced that it will be implemented from July 10th.

Public Works Bureau 72

Repairing the Hengfeng Bridge Frame

Vehicles Prohibited During the Period

The Municipal Public Works Bureau determined that the old bridge frame of the Hengfeng Bridge north of the canal was too damaged to bear the load and specifically scheduled repairs to begin on the 27th of this month. It will take about a month to complete. During the repair period, all rickshaws, small carts, and passenger cars are prohibited from passing, except for pedestrians, who can still pass. They should use the Wuzhen Bridge and the Xinzha Bridge on the east side to avoid hindering the work.

Two Handguns Seized from Two Locations

Tan Linqiang confessed that he was 25 years old, from Jiangdu, and lived in a flat in Zhang Family Residence, Carter Road. All suspects readily admitted the crimes. Verdict in Police Officer Accusation Case 80

Tao Jinqing Sentenced to Two Years Imprisonment, Suspended

Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ge of the Special District Local Court conducted a joint trial. According to Xu's testimony, Tao first came to demand 12 yuan for a small cart fee on May 10th, and when he didn't get it, he came again in the evening to pick a quarrel and beat him. Tao testified that because the rickshaw pullers at Xu's construction site were not following orders, he had confiscated their carts and taken them to the police station, which angered Xu. On that day, while he was patrolling near the construction site, Xu suddenly insulted him. When he argued with him, Xu assaulted him and damaged his uniform, so he arrested him. Because he tried to escape en route, Wang helped to handcuff him and take him to the police station. He denied extorting money. Xi and Wang completely denied the accusations against them. However, a Guo-surname shoemaker testified that he had witnessed Tao extorting money from Xu when he was delivering shoes to Xu's place that day. After hearing the testimonies, Judge Ge sentenced Tao Jinqing to two months imprisonment, suspended for two years. Tao was also allowed to post 200 yuan bail during the appeal period. Xi and Wang were acquitted.

Investigation into Wang Cailang's Strangulation Case 81

Shi Shunqing Admits to the Crime

Wang Cailang, a native of Chongming, was suddenly strangled to death on the night of the 18th of this month at 9:30 PM in the wilderness of Kunming Road, Taopeng Road. The murderer fled. Only at 2:30 PM the day before yesterday did Detective Su Changsheng of the Huishan Police Station apprehend Shi Shunqing, also from Chongming, at the home of Chen Wu, a Chongming woman, at No. 69 Shenjiatan, Yangshupu. Chen Wu was also arrested in connection. Yesterday morning, they were brought before Judge Feng of the Special District Local Court for investigation. Detective Su presented three ropes, a blue rope taken from the deceased's hands and a white rope used to strangle his neck, as evidence. Shi Shunqing testified that Wang Cailang had previously borrowed five yuan from him. On that day, he and two others who were at large demanded repayment from him at the scene of the incident. Wang said that Shi's job at the pharmacy, where he earned a monthly salary of seven yuan, was due to Wang's recommendation and refused to repay the debt, even uttering harsh words. Shi, in a fit of anger, used the ropes with the others to first tie his hands and then strangle his neck. He only intended to scare him, but Wang said that if he wasn't killed, he would beat them to death in the future. He then punched Wang in the waist until he died, then dumped the body in the nearby latrine. Chen Wu testified that her husband's name was Chen Zifang. On the day of the incident, she was cooking dinner when she heard the deceased and Shi arguing about debt outside her house in the third alley. Three days later, her husband told her that Wang had been murdered by Shi, and when she asked how he knew, her husband said that Shi had told him. But she and her husband were afraid, so they moved to Shenjiatan. Shi then claimed that the deceased's original surname was Lu and that he had committed a crime and changed his surname to Wang. Judge Feng reviewed the testimonies and ordered Chen Wu to be released first, but she was not allowed to leave Shanghai. Shi was detained pending a scheduled sentencing.

The Predicament of Dressing as a Man 83

Driven by the Need for Food and Clothing

At around 6:30 PM yesterday, a police officer from a Public Security Bureau in the Fifth District of Zhabei discovered a woman dressed in men's clothing walking on Xingjia Bridge, Gonghe Lou area. The officer arrested her for dressing as a man, which was considered to be detrimental to public morals. During interrogation, the woman stated that her name was Yu Wu, a native of Ningbo, 45 years old. She said that she dressed as a man for the convenience of street vending and requested leniency. Director Zhao, finding her circumstances pitiable, released her at the time.

Sustained Serious Head Injuries, Life in Critical Condition

At around 9 PM last night, a Huishan Motor Company car with license number 18024 caused an accident at the intersection of Broadway Road and Wuchang Road, injuring a pedestrian who sustained serious head injuries and fell to the ground unable to speak. Patrolman No. 1482 of the Hongkou Police Station arrested the driver, Xu A'si, and transported the injured person to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Dalian Steamship Company Merges with South Manchuria Railway 86

Actively Pursuing Shipping Business in China

Shanghai Ship Ticket Prices Soar

The Japanese-owned Dalian Steamship Company in this port has been taken over by the South Manchuria Railway due to the implementation of new policies. For a time, there were rumors in society that it would be dissolved. However, it is not known that the Japanese have always held the ambition to take every inch in China's shipping industry. The company is now at the start of its upturn in business so it would rather not give up its shipping rights in China. The details I have heard of the factual situation are as follows:

Changing the Name: Dalian Steamship Company was founded with the capital of the South Manchuria Railway. Currently, it has five routes: Andong, Yingkou, Tianjin, Shanghai-Dalian, Dalian-Japan. There are more than 30 ships in total. The Shanghai route is the most developed. This time, the South Manchuria Railway will be under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Railways. The method is to abolish the head office of Dalian and change it to the Shipping Department, while the outer shops will remain in operation as usual.

There will be no change in business, but there will be a change in name. It was heard yesterday that the company received a message from the South Manchuria Railway that it may be renamed the Shanghai Branch of the South Manchuria Railway Shipping Department. At the same time, it is also planned to retain the words "Dalian Steamship Company" and attach them to the name of the firm so that passengers and cargo owners will not be misled and is being discussed.

Setting up a Branch in Hong Kong: During this change of management, the shipping industry is still taking an active attitude. As the newly built ships will all be completed before September, the planned opening of the South China route will also be before September. Therefore, it is currently preparing to set up a Hong Kong branch to manage the ship schedules, passengers, and cargo in the South China ports. The branch manager has already been sent out and will be able to come to Shanghai from Dalian and transfer to Hong Kong soon.

Ticket Prices Rise Again: The Shanghai-Qingdao-Dalian ticket price of the company has already been raised once. Yesterday, another telegram was received from the Dalian head office stating that the price of gold is increasing day by day, so all cabin classes will be increased by another 20% starting from July 1st. The new prices are as follows: Shanghai to Dalian: First class was originally 60 yuan, then increased to 72 yuan, and will increase to 90 yuan on July 1st. Third class was originally 15 yuan, then increased to 18 yuan, and will increase to 22 yuan on July 1st. Shanghai to Qingdao: First class was originally 42 yuan, increased to 50 yuan, and will increase to 60 yuan on July 1st. Third class was originally 10 yuan, then increased to 12 yuan, and will increase to 15 yuan on July 1st.

Report on Lost Ship 87

Nagasaki Maru Suspended for Repairs: The Nagasaki Maru of the Japan Mail Steamship Company was sailing from Japan to Shanghai when its machinery was damaged in the Goto Islands sea area. It was temporarily repaired at the time, which resulted in a one-day delay. After returning to Japan, it set sail from Japan on the 23rd, but its machinery broke down again in the Yellow Sea. It turned back to the Eastern Ocean and dared not sail, causing it to miss its scheduled trip yesterday. A telegram was received from the head office stating that the ship has entered Dahan for major repairs and will not be able to sail until July 7th. All cargo and passengers on that ship have been ordered to be transferred to the Shanghai Maru on the 27th, and the Nagasaki Maru will be temporarily suspended for two weeks.

Wanliu Wheel Hits Reef: Taikoo Company's upper river steamer Wanliu was suspended from sailing in Shanghai due to the upper river workers' strike until May. Yesterday, the company received a telegram from Yichang stating that the Wanliu hit a reef 45 miles downstream of Chongqing on the 22nd of this month. River water had entered the cargo hold, and the bottom of the ship had also been breached, making the situation quite dangerous. The Nisshin Kisen Kaisha's upper river steamers Yunyang Maru and Peiling Maru happened to be passing through the area on their way from Yi to Yu and have now stopped to help with the rescue. It is reported that all passengers on the Wanliu have been rescued. After receiving the news, the company ordered tugboats to be dispatched from Yichang and Chongqing to the accident site to help unload the cargo. The British Navy on the upper river also sent a ship to protect the site to prevent bandits from looting.

Expansion of Shanghai Printing and Dyeing Company 89

Since its founding in the winter of the 17th year, the Shanghai Printing and Dyeing Company has purchased more than ten acres of land at Gaolang Bridge, Huade Road, to build a factory and install all the equipment. The layout is very complete. The printing and dyeing of various flower labels, satins, linen yarns, wool silk fabrics, Dantanshi Lin patriotic cloth, etc., are all striving for perfection. In April and May, the purchase of machines has significantly increased the production rate, with an average daily output of more than 3,500 pieces. The general manager of the company, Mr. Zhang Rongchu, convened a meeting of the directors, who believed that the company's operations were very promising. However, silk products, which account for a portion of sales in the printing and dyeing industry, were still lacking, and the profits of the printing and dyeing industry were still leaking overseas. Therefore, it was proposed to add silk machines and other ancillary equipment to ensure that the products would be all-encompassing, so as to achieve the goal of truly resisting foreign goods. In addition, in order to expand the scope of business, the company's board of directors decided to continue to raise 250,000 yuan in stock. In addition to the 150,000 yuan subscribed by the directors, the remaining 100,000 yuan will be reserved for shareholders to publicly subscribe before convening the shareholders' meeting. It is reported that those from all walks of life who are interested in this industry can also subscribe.

Preparatory Meeting for the Reorganization of the Shanghai Paint Industry Association 90

The Shanghai Special Municipality Paint Industry Association held a preparatory meeting for reorganization at the association's premises at Xue Lane at 2 PM the day before yesterday. More than 20 people attended. The documents were reported by Min Xingchu, who reported the purpose of the meeting. Ni Fusheng was publicly elected as the chairman, and Xiao Peisheng, Du Gengsheng, Zhang Shanjin, Pan Pingsan, Zhang Fukang, Zhang Youshui, etc., were elected as standing committee members. The remaining eight people, including Xu Shunrong, Xu Shuitang, and Wang Shengcai, were all executive committee members. The following proposals were then discussed: (1) Ratification of the appointment of Du Gengsheng, Zhang Fukang, Zhang Shanjin, and Zhang Youshui as representatives to attend the Business Reorganization Conference. Resolution passed. (2) The official establishment date of the association. It was resolved to complete the membership list and revise the regulations and articles of association before July 10 of this year in order to officially report to the party and government agencies to send personnel for guidance. (3) Those colleagues who have not yet completed their application forms are required to submit them to the store by the deadline. Those who fail to do so will be deemed to be deliberately resisting the resolution and will be submitted to the Social Bureau for sanctions. Next, the documents were reported by Min Xingchu, who reported the various procedures for handling the association's affairs. In fact, most of the paint industry colleagues do not understand the matter. For this registration, there were as many as four or five circulars, but they were ignored. As Mr. Wang Xiaolai said at the Business Reorganization Conference, the first step in reorganization is registration, but registration is an innovation in this city's merchants, so many people do not take it seriously. Second, organizations that are not legally organized should be transformed into legal entities. Those with the same nature should be merged, but those who have been accustomed to letting go in the past are now seriously implementing it, and there will inevitably be some difficulties. I am really exhausted and exhausted in the reorganization and registration of this association, and there are no achievements to record. Please ask all the gentlemen present to elect another virtuous person to assist in the progress. Everyone agreed and publicly elected Mr. Zhang Fukang as a member of the Paint and Woodenware Industry Reorganization Committee. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Jing'an Epidemic Hospital to be Established in West Shanghai 91

The Jing'an Temple area in West Shanghai is a prosperous commercial area with a large number of residents, especially laborers. The area lacks an epidemic prevention hospital for relief. Many members of the Jing'an Temple Board of Directors and the Business Federation, as well as party member Gong Yifei, have recognized this and initiated the organization of a temporary hospital near the Jing'an Temple. A large building has been located for the hospital site, which is named the Jing'an Epidemic Hospital. It will engage in prevention, rescue, medical treatment, and dispensing medicine so that patients can receive nearby treatment. The hospital is currently raising funds from all walks of life.

Free Talk

Hu Puan Promotes National Martial Arts Ma Xieguo 94

Since taking office this spring, the Director of the Jiangsu Civil Affairs Department, Mr. Hu Puan, has been striving to improve internal and external affairs. Therefore, the Civil Affairs Department has the most proposals at each meeting of the Provincial Government. Mr. Hu used to be a professor at various universities in Shanghai, enjoying himself with books and also studying Xingyi and Bagua boxing, which he considered to be normal. After taking charge of the government of Jiangsu, he has been busy with official duties and has no time to sort out ancient books, but he has never interrupted his practice of boxing. Yesterday, I met with a friend who told me in great detail about Mr. Hu's recent situation, so I recorded it to share in this column.

Mr. Hu Puan is from Jing County, Anhui Province. His residence is in Yuntaishan, Zhenjiang South Ma Road, my hometown. The scenery there is excellent and the decorations are quite elegant. Every morning when the sky is slightly bright, Mr. Hu must first practice Bagua boxing for several sets on the hillside road to cultivate his body and mind and absorb fresh air. At 7 o'clock, he goes to the Civil Affairs Department to teach boxing until 8 o'clock. Those who join include the section chief of the Secretariat and section members, totaling fifty people, divided into elementary and advanced levels. The elementary level is taught by Mr. Liu from the National Martial Arts Hall, while the advanced level is taught by Mr. Hu himself. Except for Sundays, when there is a routine rest, there has never been any interruption. It is heard that Mr. Hu also serves as the director of the Jiangsu Provincial National Martial Arts Hall. A few days ago, he discussed with Mr. Ye Chucang, the chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, to continue running the second phase of the women's training class in the National Martial Arts Hall, mainly to eliminate bad habits and develop women's physical education. Both Mr. Ye and Mr. Hu are enthusiastic about promoting national martial arts and are planning for the balanced development of physical education for both men and women.

Meeting of the Commercial Readjustment Committee Convening Representatives from Various Industries 95

Reported by Sun Choucheng

Since the National Government's Ministry of Industry and Commerce revised the Chamber of Commerce Law, chambers of commerce across the country have reorganized accordingly. On the 21st of this month, the Shanghai Commercial Readjustment Committee convened a conference of representatives from all industry guilds in the city to elect executive and supervisory committee members in accordance with the new Chamber of Commerce Law, thereby establishing the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce. This meeting has garnered attention from chambers of commerce nationwide. Therefore, despite the tediousness, we have recorded the details omitted by other newspapers as follows:

Attendance and Verification: To ensure solemnity due to the presence of over 300 members on this day, the committee issued attendance certificates in advance, detailing the guild name, representative name, and assigned number. The certificates were stamped, and the number matched the seat number in the venue. Members were required to present the certificate upon arrival, after which they were issued a badge and printed materials such as the agenda.

Overview of the Venue: The venue was located on the second floor, with seating arranged in three rows and fourteen columns. Each long table had nine seats, covered with a white tablecloth and equipped with natural ink, blotter, notebook, a writing brush, a pencil, and a teacup. A horizontal banner with golden characters on a red background hung above, and a table in the center served as the chairman's platform. Representatives from various agencies were seated beneath the portrait of Sun Yat-sen, while the recording staff sat to the right of the platform.

Badge Identification: The badges issued by the committee on this day were all made of ribbon, approximately five inches long, and featured the emblem of the Blue Sky with a White Sun. They were available in three colors: light red, dark red, and natural color. Light red badges bore the words "Presidium," dark red badges read "Member Representative," and natural color badges indicated titles such as "Master of Ceremonies," "Recorder," "Discipline Officer," and "Receptionist," worn on the chest.

Wang Xiaolai's Busy Schedule: Wang Xiaolai, a standing committee member of the Commercial Readjustment Committee, served as one of the members of the presidium on this day. He delivered the opening address in a loud voice, reminiscent of his portrayal of Yao Qi in the "Caoqiao Pass" opera. During the discussion of the regulations, photography was done in advance. Due to the large venue, the speaker was photographed from the stage, and two more photos were taken of the representatives from the left and right sides of the stage. All matters related to light and exposure were directed by Mr. Wang, who was seen running around busily.

Yu Qiaqing's Absence: The name Yu Qiaqing is known to all, from women and children, with a knowing smile... --Haiket

A: What have you been up to lately?

B: I've been extremely busy these past few days. I haven't had a moment to spare, barely even enough time to eat.

A: The capable are always busy, that's for sure. But what exactly are you so busy with?

B: I'm busy looking for a decent job because I've been unemployed for quite a while.

Father: Students at school often give each other nicknames. What's your nickname at school, son?

Son: They call me "Grass Roots."

Father: That's a rather peculiar nickname. Do you know what it means?

Son: Because I always rank at the bottom of the class in every exam, and grass roots are always at the bottom too.

A: Who are the greatest people in the world?

B: Barbers.

A: Barbers are considered a lowly profession. How can you call them the greatest people in the world?

B: Don't you see? No matter how high and mighty the important figures of the world are, they all have to bow their heads under the hands of a barber.

He is also a standing committee member of the Commercial Readjustment Committee. His absence on this day was a surprise to many. It is believed that Mr. Yu, due to his extensive public service, was concerned about being elected as an executive committee member due to his exhaustion. Therefore, when the shipping guild nominated representatives, he instructed his son, Shunmao, to take his place, withdrawing himself from consideration. He not only abstained from attending on this day but also relinquished his eligibility for election.

Busy Hands, Steady Feet: There is an old saying in China, "busy hands, chaotic feet." On this day, the meeting started at 9:00 AM and lasted until 6:00 PM. The representatives sat still for six hours, rendering their feet useless. A full course meal was served at noon and eaten at their seats to save time. They ate and discussed simultaneously. During voting, they had to put down their knives and forks to raise their hands. When electing executive and supervisory committee members, they had to personally fill in the names of the candidates. Thus, the work of the hands and feet was vastly different on this day.

In Memoriam: Mr. Cheng Dihua, Renowned Proofreader of Shanghai 96

By Ling Shanqing

Mr. Cheng had served as a proofreader at the Great Eastern Book Company for nearly ten years. His scholarly achievements were considerable, and he was diligent in his work. Mr. Shou Juan even referred to him as the "King of Proofreading." Unfortunately, he fell from a building and died on the 8th of this month, a great loss indeed. That day was a day off. Mr. Cheng returned to his residence in the late evening, slightly inebriated. He went upstairs to bed. Around 10:00 PM, a colleague in the next room heard the ringing of the bell in the workshop. Feeling strange, he crept over and saw Mr. Cheng lying near the staircase after falling. He quickly called for help. However, due to concussion and cerebral congestion, Mr. Cheng passed away suddenly. The rope of the bell hammer was attached to the handrail of the stairs. It is presumed that Mr. Cheng grabbed the rope while falling, but his grip failed, causing the bell to ring. Yesterday was the day of Mr. Cheng's funeral. I hereby compose two elegiac couplets in his memory:

First couplet: "Confined in a pharmacy like a dragon, a tipsy moment leading to an accidental fall, causing eternal regret; In a perilous building, riding the crane at midnight, hearing the alarm, most startling is the sound of a bell."

Second couplet: "Acquainted for twenty years, working together for ten years, admiring your extensive learning, I once asked you about rare characters; Surpassing sixty years of age, life ending in a moment, proofreading scriptures into a final masterpiece, Heaven mourning the loss of such a cultured man due to the fall."

Reading [The Vanguard Weekly] 97

By Yang Feiwo

As the National Revolution progresses, the new literature is declining. All that can be seen in the modern literary world are either classical literature of the aristocratic class singing loudly or proletarian literature shouting with all their might. What we feel is disappointment and sorrow, lamenting the decline of both new and old literature. Unexpectedly, in the disappointing and sorrowful declining modern literary world, we are able to obtain unexpected dawn. How should we cheer and celebrate?

I have long heard that the Nationalist literary movement is actively progressing with effort, and their publication came into being on the 22nd of this month. Although in terms of quantity, it is only a four-page newspaper size, which seems to be very weak, but upon investigating its content, it can already express their mission, enthusiastic and brave spirit, and it really has the spirit to save the decline of Chinese literature.

The inaugural issue of Vanguard has a total of seven articles, including [The Decline of Chinese Literature], [The Relationship Between Nationalism and Literature], [Mr. Lu Xun's Foresight], [The Way to Make Money Qian Xingcun], [The So-called Slaves of Doctrine], [Charms and Sorcerers], and a launch speech. In the two articles [The Decline of Chinese Literature] and [The Relationship Between Nationalism and Literature], the path to saving Chinese literature is revealed. Old literature has declined, and new literature has not been able to completely fall. We must not allow it to decline. If we are going to not have it naturally, we should muster an enduring spirit and work hard on the literary revolution, that is, work hard on the nationalist literary movement and walk the bright road we should take. After reading these two works, we may be able to understand the correct theory of literature and recognize the way out for Chinese literature.

At the same time, in addition to promoting their theory, [The Vanguard] also reveals the true face of Proletarian writers as much as possible. In the four articles [Mr. Lu Xun's Foresight], [The Way to Make Money Qian Xingcun], [The So-called Slaves of Doctrine], [Charms and Sorcerers], we can understand what the Proletarian writers were like. This is their characteristic and their spirit. The article [The Relationship Between Nationalism and Literature] clearly states [It is not permissible for anything that is bad or harms the nation, no matter which class it belongs to, the Nationalist literature must be conscious of and reject it] [In short, Nationalist literature is literature that promotes the national spirit from the national position, is hopeful and powerful, and as for critical literature, it is literature that grasps the spirit of the times]. After reading this conclusion, we can better understand their purpose and spirit. The silent Chinese literary world and the declining Chinese literature has produced this new force in modern times. It is naturally the savior of Chinese literature, awakening the literary world to recognize the consciousness of their own nation.

News: The wedding of Mr. Wei Zhuyi and Ms. 眖君 is scheduled to take place on the 29th of this month in the auditorium of the Great China Hotel. The Ya Jing Society will stage a song and dance drama and a new drama, and the Ya Ji Society amateurs will perform Peking Opera selections such as "Cailou Pei Tuo Zhao," "Peng Sui Da Yan Song," the full version of "Hong Luan Xi," the full version of "Fenghuang Shan," and the full version of "Yu Bei Ting," all of which are excellent works (if any).

Chapter 12: Farewell Banquet, Lingering Flower Shadows; Fine Garden Gathering, Tasting Tea, Viewing Beauty

Afterwards, Zuo Shichen asked Ruiyun for another photo as a memento. Ruiyun said, "Didn't I have several photos taken at the Mingjing Photography Studio with you? Then she immediately changed her tone and said, "Okay, I'll go take some tomorrow. Do you want a full-body or a half-body?" Zuo Shichen wanted a half-body one. She asked A Jin, "Is it better to have braids for the photo shoot tomorrow?" I believe braiding my hair makes me look older."

At this meal, Ruiyun didn't say much at first, but then she stopped being silent. Regarding her marriage, she preferred to marry a few years later, but she couldn't decide for herself. She believed that when she was at home in Nanjing, her body belonged to her parents. When the old woman Wang bought her to be a child bride, the ownership of her body belonged to the old woman Wang. When she was sold to the big aunt, who called her "mother," she became the big aunt's person. She had no choice but to do as she was told. As for the choice of a good man to marry, she had no say either. For example, when she was taken by the old woman Wang to be a child bride, her fiancé was much older than her and was the most annoying, naughty, and hateful person. If she hadn't been sold by the old woman Wang and had been forced to marry this most hated fiancé, it would have been something to be expected. Her heart was empty, and she had nothing to cling to. Although she was around men all day long, she said that she mechanically delivered a few platitudes in her essays and mechanically performed a few actions. For example, if someone wanted to kiss her face, her face would be stiff and the stinky beard would prick her tender cheeks. She could avoid it if she could, but if it was unavoidable and had to be carried out by force, she could only suppress her disgust, frown, and reluctantly let them relieve this hunger, as if singing a song in the hall meant she had the obligation to let them kiss her face for an unknown amount of foreign money. She felt that being forced was nothing. Although she was like a petal of spring, scattered in the hearts of men, she still did not have a lovely opposite sex. At the dinner party, there was a fleeting glimpse. She ran around fifty or sixty times a night, and by twelve o'clock, she was exhausted. A special express letter had already been sent to her pillow, urging her to go to the black sweet village. Tomorrow night would be the same. Many guests had already asked her to sing three or four times, but she still couldn't call out their last names. Fortunately, the adjutant A Jin had a strong memory. Her mind was a hall ledger. On the first day of the month, this guest asked Ruiyun to call him again on the fifteenth of next month, and A Jin remembered it clearly.

Commercial News

Finance

Golden Tide Overwhelming

Terrifying Bearishness, Prospects for Further Gains

Missing Invoices, Rare Peaks Emerge: Yesterday, the gold market once again experienced a turbulent and tidal wave. The rapid changes were unpredictable, with a fluctuating price of two to four taels. It seemed like madness. The day was filled with twists and turns, reaching seven taels, and new peaks emerged frequently, causing alarm. The barrier of 620 taels was once again breached. As for foreign exchange, the selling pressure seemed to lessen, but brokers were unsure of the standard. Consequently, transactions were conducted with caution, selling and buying alternately. Only Zhifeng Yong, Dada Cheng, Changsheng Yong, and others were slightly bullish, while Hengxing Yucheng Yongtaixing sold off. The market opened slightly lower due to the slight decrease in silver prices. Later, buyers became active, reaching 22 taels, but sellers appeared to be more numerous. With the decline in foreign exchange, the market turned weak, especially in the afternoon, breaking through 615 taels. Afterwards, buyers reappeared with agility, but the supply was scarce. Due to the high demand and lack of invoices, the market surged, surpassing the morning's high, reaching 622 taels and two cents. However, due to the lack of market on Wednesday, short sellers became extremely fearful. They were greatly stimulated and fear that a new high price will reappear in the future.

Opened high and then turned soft: Yesterday, the big invoices have dropped sixteen-thirds and the silver market has also reduced one-quarter. The August gold price opened at 618 taels, a slight decrease of eight cents. It then jumped up four taels, a total of twenty-two taels. However, sellers took advantage of this high price to sell, resulting in a five tael drop. When the first order was issued, the price was 17 taels and two cents. However, the listed price has been reduced by half of the price, a total of 125 US dollars, a reduction of 25. The price of gold rose one cent to eighteen taels and two cents. Then, because Hengxing and other companies sold, and the price of each exchange transaction was not tight, the price fell by one tael, for a total of seventeen taels. After this, Sumitomo and Zhejiang did the next month's Citibank at 35.9375 yuan, and someone entered the invoice, and suddenly rushed up three taels to 20 taels and 0.12 cents. At that time, HSBC and Zhejiang each did the next month's Citibank at 36 yuan. The people’s hearts were hit hard, and the price was about 18 taels and 12 cents around 10 o'clock. After more than ten minutes, the price rose more than one tael, which was bought by a certain speculator, so it was 19 taels and 8 cents. At 10:30, all the shops were sold out, and the people's hearts went down, and the market was tired, and the situation was getting worse and worse. There was a rise and fall of two taels until five taels before 11:45. Finally, it fell to 14 taels and five cents. Afterwards, there was a rise and fall of more than one tael until noon. The price was 15 and a half taels. It was possible to buy a tael of gold for 1 tael, 3 cents and 8 points. Also, the first order was 5 pence and 8125. The price was changed to 672 taels and 6 cents. It was estimated that the price was small. 54 to 55 taels to 56.7 taels.

At night, it hit 22 taels and 2 cents. The market opened at 16 taels and 9 cents. The items opened at 16 taels and 8 cents. After that, it went up to the clouds for a total of 17 taels and 8 cents. There seemed to be more sellers, so the price fell back by 2 taels to 15.78 cents at 3:00. After that, the head strips came to scramble to buy. Zhifeng Yong and others also followed and chased. It almost rose a thousand feet. The sharp market was so sharp that the suppliers were silent and avoided it. The people were panicking and the shorts were quickly replenished. The long side added code and all went the same way. It has already risen by six taels to another. Finally, it was pushed to 622 taels and 2 cents, but there was no market for drafts, so it was Tuesday. At the close at 4:30, it was estimated that the closing price of 22 taels was continuing to rise by 3 taels and 3 cents compared to the previous day. Check the maximum price of 22 taels and 2 cents in one day. The minimum price is 14 taels and 5 cents, which is 7 taels and 7 cents apart. The items opened at 18 taels in the morning, closed at 16 taels at noon, 6 taels and 8 cents in the afternoon, and closed at 22 taels. The prices are more than ten taels lower than local yarn. Merchants from Sichuan and other inland provinces have been continuously purchasing large quantities. In the midst of this war and turmoil, the accumulation of stagnant inventory is a growing concern. Coupled with the invasion of cheap Japanese yarn, the future is truly bleak.

Various Perspectives on the Grain and Flour Market Downstream

Yesterday, the flour market unanimously softened again in both the morning and afternoon for all months. While this reversal from rise to fall was partly due to the terrible drop in foreign wheat prices (Chicago fell to a minimum of 8.8 jiao, a further drop of about 1.23 yuan from the previous day), the biggest impact was actually the unusually abundant harvest of new wheat in the northern provinces this year. Currently, Tianjin has no market for Shanghai flour due to unsuitability, and local factories are fully supplying the demand. If this trend continues, the factories' sales channels will inevitably be hit unexpectedly. As a result, factories have been dumping their goods more actively, and external bulls are also gradually withdrawing, causing the market to fall step by step in all months. As a result, this month fell by another 1.75 fen compared to the previous day, July fell by 2 fen, August fell by 2.25 fen, September fell by 2.25 fen, October fell by 2 fen, and November fell by 2.5 fen.

Spot Wheat Increases Bidding Again 104

Futures Near Steady, Distant Months Weaker

Yesterday, the rice market this month saw rising sentiment as customers replenished their positions, while the distant months were weak due to low prices of foreign wheat. If sluggish sales continue, the market may remain weak. As a result, this month was better by 4 fen compared to the previous day, August remained unchanged, September was down by 1 fen, and October and November were down by 2 fen. Spot wheat, with factories taking a wait-and-see approach, continued to increase bidding again, and all grades were down by another 5 fen. High, You, Shao, Yangzhou, Shishan, Penglai, Chongming, Jinpu Railway and other new and old wheat totaling over 13,000 bags.

Foreign Rice Flat in the Morning, Rises in the Afternoon 105

Yesterday, foreign rice saw a weak trend before the market opened due to the arrival of new shipments and several more ships expected to arrive within one or two days and at the end of the month. Subsequently, the market turned better as local inland and Zhejiang merchants actively purchased, with total transactions exceeding 20,000 bags. Sentiment improved, and merchants from Wenzhou, Taizhou, and Ningbo competed to purchase, while Hunan Changsha also made purchases, causing prices to rise by 1 jiao. Transactions included 3,000 bags of No. 1 Saigon, 4,000 bags of No. 2, 5,000 bags of small broken rice, 4,000 bags of large broken rice, 2,000 bags of end-of-month delivery, 1,000 bags of Kergay rice, 1,000 bags of Min Dang rice, and 3,000 bags of small broken rough rice for end-of-month delivery.

The Rice Market at Hexia Is Virtually Stalled 106

Due to Unfinished Registration and Appraisal Procedures

Yesterday, ship cargoes were very scarce in Shanbei, with only a few shipments. Rice ships undergoing registration could not be appraised due to the absence of some cargo owners from Shanghai. At the same time, rice shops registered their purchases separately at the association for fair distribution, so that the prices could be determined and allocated for transport to Beigeng tomorrow. The decision was made to handle top-grade cargo at the maximum price of 21 yuan. As a result, all procedures were not yet completed, and the transaction of both Keng and Bo markets was virtually stalled throughout the day. Only Biangeng saw minor transactions, with no significant gains or losses.

The Keng rice market at Hexia in South Shanghai still saw no arrivals, and only a few top-grade Bo rice shipments were available. Transactions were mainly dominated by foreign rice. All very fine Yangjian rice and Tongbiangeng rice were sought after due to their scarcity. The overall market remained firm, with top-grade Yangjian reaching 20.05 yuan and top-grade Biangeng around 20 yuan. Reports from the railway indicate that the market prices in Suzhou and Wuxi are also tight, making it difficult to establish connections with the local market for the time being.

The silk sales in Lyon still show no improvement, and the New York silk telegrams are also scarce due to the shrinking exchange rate. The market atmosphere is bleak.
