Decline in European Sales of Zhenmei Green Tea 108

Zhenmei tea, a major product among green teas, has suffered a continuous decline in European sales since the new tea season began. Recently, although small amounts of high-grade tea from Gaoshuang in northern Wuyuan County have been sold upon arrival, the quantities are insignificant and do not affect the overall situation. A substantial inventory of 30,000 boxes from Tunxi, Suian, Shexian, and other regions has accumulated. The sluggish sales of Zhenmei tea are unprecedented in recent years. Yesterday, it was reported that Zhenmei tea from Tunxi had already entered the interior market at 100 taels. The decline of the market is evident. However, there is news that the head manager of the Xiezhuhui will arrive in Shanghai on the 28th. If Russian firms actively start procuring Zhenmei tea, the declining trend in the market might be reversed.

Yuan velvet has been heavily invested in by merchants along the street.

Top-grade seeds have already increased by 2.5 taels, while medium and lower grades have also increased by 1 to 2 taels. Production areas such as Henan Province are expected to have scarce production due to war, and Xuzhou has also suffered from flooding, making a good harvest difficult. June 26th, Year 19 of the Republic of China (Shanghai News Supplement) Thursday (2)

Arts and Culture

Literature and Art and National Consciousness by Ying Peng

Recently, some colleagues have been working hard to awaken [national consciousness] through literature and art. This has given rise to a strong vitality in contemporary literature and art, and it is inevitable that it has aroused resonance. Now, I will publish some of my usual notes on national consciousness and literature and art. Of course, these notes were written without a precise system, so I can only publish them here day by day. I plan to organize them into a complete piece when I have the opportunity.

(1)

If one is not clear-headed when discussing the nationalist literary movement in China, one will certainly misunderstand it as [preserving the national essence]. This is indeed a great mistake. Not everything in China can be called [essence]. Most of it may be [dross]. The literature and art created by Chinese intellectuals are nothing more than the expression of three kinds of thought: a desire for fame and wealth, a pessimistic view of the world, and a belief in fate. All three of these are centered on the individual and have nothing to do with the nation. Such thoughts should be extremely rejected from the standpoint of the nation.

The period of the feudal system in Chinese history was too long, perhaps because the organization of Chinese feudal politics was more complete and precise than that of Europe. As a result, the philosophy of yin and yang and the five elements and the doctrine of the mean became the center of Chinese culture. The outlook on life applicable under the feudal system was to cultivate oneself, regulate one's family, govern the state, and pacify the world. This was clearly positioning oneself in the position of ruler and controller, so all culture under the feudal system was fundamentally not national culture.

The organization of the Chinese family system was indeed initially based on the spirit of the nation, but because of the match of feudal politics and the assimilation of rationalist philosophy, it became a deformed and morbid development. As a result, the narrow patriarchal social organization became increasingly strict, and its foundation became increasingly solid, while the national spirit disappeared instead. Therefore, the [way of being a person] for educated Chinese people, outside of the family, was either the individual or the world. The so-called clan consciousness only had a momentary manifestation when oppressed by foreign races, but it would disappear again after a very short period.

China has undergone several conquests by foreign races, but the national consciousness still has considerable reserves among the people. Although the form of government has been reformed since the Xinhai Revolution, feudal forces remain consolidated. In particular, those in power absolutely ignore the thoughts, actions, organization, and hobbies of the people. They continue to prohibit folk entertainment and gatherings, and they continue to suppress folk songs and legends. Those who study folklore mistake it for ethnology. Those who study folklore do not focus their research on [national consciousness] and do not think about how to excavate the treasure of [national consciousness] hidden among the people. This is truly strange. Of course, Chinese folk entertainment or gatherings, folk songs or legends, inevitably still contain some remnants of escapist thought and feudal thought. However, relatively speaking, such elements are certainly less in the works of the so-called scholar-officials. We should stand on the point of the national spirit and carefully dissect and distinguish, taking what is useful and discarding what is not. In this regard, we must not dismiss everything with a single stroke, otherwise we will be destroying our own national spirit.

We have seen great evidence of the [national consciousness] contained in folk thought from the secret societies of the Jianghu, from the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom, from the Boxers, and from all the movements of the Xingzhonghui. A seed of [national consciousness] finally blossomed into the flower of the Chinese nation after drifting for a certain period and in a certain place. It is unimaginable that such a precious thing has always been buried and not heeded by intellectuals, and it is not yet heeded by intellectuals even now. [National consciousness] is collective, upward-looking, positive, striving, and creative. All of these are produced from the purpose of fighting for survival, fighting for freedom, and fighting for prosperity. Therefore, we see folk thoughts and actions, folk songs and legends, and everything else. If they have this nature, then they should of course be regarded as national treasures.

After thousands of years of oppression, the development of the [national consciousness] of the Chinese nation has undergone many difficulties and setbacks. The seeds buried among the people have not yet become widespread, and intellectuals, in particular, should have an urgent awakening.

The Complete Works of George Bernard Shaw by Kehua

The world-renowned seventy-three-year-old playwright George Bernard Shaw recently announced through his book dealers that a complete collection of his works will be published. The collection will be printed in thirty volumes, including all of his major works throughout his life. The first four volumes will be published in July of this year, and the rest will be published successively every few months. The entire collection will be completed by the end of next year.

The most valuable aspect of this complete collection is that it includes all of his earliest and most recent efforts. The first volume is his novel [Immaturity], written when he was twenty-two years old, which was rejected by various book dealers. He wrote a very long preface, explaining the circumstances of the book's publication in his best politeness. From this book, critics will immediately determine that the style of the seventy-three-year-old famous writer is incomparable to that of other immature literary authors.

This complete collection also includes Shaw's recent play [The Apple Cart], which has not only been successfully staged in London but has also been staged in other major cities. An even more interesting question is his collection of letters and pamphlets on the discussion of war. The publication of this book will surely be valued by collectors because it is the only purely uniform book of Shaw's works. This world-famous author has been living happily on his pen for forty years, and now his life's masterpieces are all contained in this complete collection.

June 26th (Shanghai News Supplement) Thursday (5)

Qingfeng Garden

After Seeing Fudan's Cyrano by Wen Juan

Fudan Drama Society has performed the famous French play [Cyrano de Bergerac] by Rostand many times. Although I am very fond of art, I am often frightened by a group of shallow and immature stage actions, so I have never had the courage to visit her resolutely. On the 19th of this month, when it was drizzling, Sister W came to me in a hurry to ask me to go to see Cyrano with her. I hesitated for a while, partly because I couldn't refuse her request, and finally picked up my raincoat and went to the New Central Theater on Haining Road. After receiving the program and reading it, I knew that the protagonist was still Mr. Ma Yanxiang, and I was very happy because my ears told me that Mr. Ma is a rare talent in the current drama circle.

The curtain opened. The costumes and actions of many knights were still not far from the script. Cyrano's appearance was like a red sun emerging from the clouds, making the whole scene more exciting. When Cyrano said, [Am I Monsieur 'No-You-Shall-Sing'?] everyone who was pointed at by his sword showed a kind of extreme fear. The few people standing at the foot of the stairs were so scared that they almost wanted to escape to the upstairs. These supporting roles were very well done. Also, when Cyrano and Valvert were fencing, Hawke's whole body in the box was trembling and his face was changing color. Although there were additional notes in the script, the actions at that time were not written clearly. These are all the careful points of the director that the audience should not ignore. There were so many people in the first act that I was initially very afraid that they would fail. However, the performance was still very satisfying. However, the flower girl's appearance was too devoid of drama and too forgetting that she was acting. The candy girl was much better, more natural and experienced.

At the end, Cyrano confided his thoughts to Le Bret. He said,

[I dream of having an arm to lean on, slowly walking in the moonlight. My thoughts are so excited that I forget all my worries, but suddenly I see my shadow appearing on the garden wall.] He walked and recited, and the expressions and actions of his face and body were sometimes affectionate and sometimes impassioned, ultimately ending in disappointed sadness. Not to mention that Le Bret in the play was moved by his words, even we in the audience were almost in tears. Later, when he accepted Hawke's promise, his surprise and confusion were also acted appropriately.

The second act was the pastry shop of the poet Ragueneau. Mr. Wu Shude, who played Ragueneau, was also very good. When those poets were reciting poems, his attitude of listening with his hands folded was very natural. He is a pastry chef and also a poet at the same time. This double-personality role is not easy to excel in, but his performance was very suitable for the personality of the character in the play.

Cyrano's infatuation and frequent checking of the time when writing letters were very profound. When Hawke said that she loved Christian, his disappointment and despair were truly sympathetic. However, this is not difficult. What is difficult is to restrain his emotions and resolutely agree to protect his rival in love. This great and sacrificial spirit can only be done by Cyrano, and our Cyrano on the stage can understand the hero's group of measures and great love in the play, making the audience feel that the person wearing a top hat and a cloak is really Cyrano. This kind of skill cannot be done by people with considerable literary cultivation.

Ms. Liang, who played Hawke, has a lot of help from her innate strengths. A kind of coquettishness of a spoiled young lady is very lovely. When there is a lack of female artistic talents, it is always rare and valuable.

The third act is the important performance of Christian. In the moonlight, our Hawke also appeared on the balcony like a fairy in the moon palace. All the dialogues were still good, but at the moment of the tragic farewell after the wedding, she seemed to lack expression too much. According to the script, when Hawke was holding onto Christian, urging Christian to leave, she rushed into Christian's arms and called Christian's name. However, she did not dare to do this, probably because she was shy. We should forgive her. As for Christian being dragged out and desperately struggling and sending her a kiss with his hand, it was very researched.

The cadet officer of the fourth act, Guasmai, can be said to be more humorous than sad. The drunkenness and starvation of many officers are quite funny. When Christian realized the failure of love and died, the humorous atmosphere changed to extreme sadness. However, Christian's disappointment and determination before his death were also acted very generously and passionately. Mr. Tang Yuanfan can also be regarded as successful. At this time, Hawke's expression still lacked tension. When a lover is injured and dying, how should one be sad and how should one be shocked? The script also has the phrase [I feel his face is cold against my face], so Hawke should at least hug him once or rub his face against him. However, she did not do this. Hawke has always lacked enthusiasm and courage from beginning to end. I don't know if it was the director's negligence or Ms. Liang herself was unwilling. Here, we can only keep it as a question.

Our Hawke in the last act was more experienced. She is probably a neurotic young lady who is suitable for acting in sad and quiet dramas. The way she was embroidering the veil and waiting for Cyrano can be said to have fully expressed all her feelings. Her facial expressions were also the best at this time. Cyrano came to say goodbye, his smile and his fatigue became more and more immersive. In the twilight of the fallen leaves and the vast nunnery, a widow wearing filial piety faced a dying old friend, and Cyrano, who combined the beauty of a poet and a swordsman, was a hero again.

Page 24

Republic of China, Year Nineteen

The late-blooming man endured the wounds of love and died momentarily. What a state it was. My tears were soaking the glass of my glasses, and I dared not look at the hero's situation before his death. How ridiculous I was! However, when Hawke discovered that Cyrano was the soul of Christian, whom she loved, there should be more twists and turns, and more actions, otherwise it would be too plain and somewhat inconsistent with the facts. I read the script carefully. When she said [That Voice!] it should have been [trembling], although this is considered a small flaw. Cyrano was about to die, and she covered her face and cried with both hands. This way of crying was very suitable for her status, because she was already a widow who had been living in the nunnery for a long time. The focus of the whole play was on this act, and it was also Ms. Liang's last successful section. As for Mr. Ma's Cyrano, it was impeccable from beginning to end. Sister Ai, who is very discerning in art, also said [Satisfied! Satisfied!]

The scenery of the whole play shows that the director has done his best. Except for some small details, it is always worthy of the original author. This overall costume and equipment probably cost the troupe a lot of money. However, when Hawke went out to the battlefield, she should have put on her hat and gloves.

Youth Garden Contribution Guidelines

(1) Articles are limited to discussions on youth issues, news of domestic and foreign schools or students, essays, descriptions of school life, essays, etc. The style is not limited.

(2) Pictures are limited to those related to youth issues.

(3) Photos are for youth life (such as sports, travel, tours)

Various competitions such as lectures, speeches, gatherings, exhibitions, etc., school news, and photography of youth movements are welcome, regardless of individuals or groups.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the paper.

(5) The number of words per article should not exceed 2,000.

(6) Do not write horizontally, and do not write carelessly. Western text can be abbreviated as much as possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.
